          --monorail-metadata-toggled-bg: var(--monorail-metadata-closed-bg);
        }
        mr-issue-page[codeFont] {
          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: flex-start;
          z-index: 200;
        }
        .container-issue-content {
          padding: 0;
          flex-grow: 1;

          box-sizing: border-box;
          padding-top: 0.5em;
        }

          box-sizing: border-box;
          width: 100%;
          max-width: 100%;
          margin: auto;
          padding: 0;
          display: flex;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: space-between;
          flex-direction: row;
          flex-wrap: no-wrap;
        }
        .container-no-issue {
          padding: 0.5em 16px;

        }
        .metadata-container {
          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);

          border-right: var(--chops-normal-border);

          width: 24em;
          min-width: 256px;
          flex-grow: 0;
          flex-shrink: 0;
          box-sizing: border-box;
          z-index: 100;
        }
        .issue-header-container {
          z-index: 10;

          top: var(--monorail-header-height);
          margin-bottom: 0.25em;
          width: 100%;
        }

          min-width: 50%;
          max-width: 1000px;
          flex-grow: 1;
          box-sizing: border-box;
          min-height: 100%;

          padding-right: var(--mr-issue-page-horizontal-padding);
        }
        mr-issue-metadata {
          position: sticky;
          overflow-y: auto;
          top: var(--monorail-header-height);
          height: calc(100vh - var(--monorail-header-height));
        }
        mr-launch-overview {
          border-left: var(--chops-normal-border);

            flex-direction: column;

          }
          mr-issue-details, mr-launch-overview {
            width: 100%;

        @media (max-width: 840px) {

          }
        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

<b class="line"><!---->Steps to reproduce the problem:<!----></b>



<br>





The problem was found by my fuzzer running on CF(CC Security team for access permission 



<span class="line"><!---->The problem was found by my fuzzer running on CF(CC Security team for access permission <!----></span>





https://clusterfuzz.com/testcase-detail/4657073883381760,https://clusterfuzz.com/testcase-detail/6355298952609792



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://clusterfuzz.com/testcase-detail/4657073883381760,https://clusterfuzz.com/testcase-detail/6355298952609792"><!---->https://clusterfuzz.com/testcase-detail/4657073883381760,https://clusterfuzz.com/testcase-detail/6355298952609792<!----></a>





),



<span class="line"><!---->),<!----></span>



<br>





But it cannot be reproduced stably, CF may not automatically report.



<span class="line"><!---->But it cannot be reproduced stably, CF may not automatically report.<!----></span>



<br>





By manual review, it is found that the window time triggered by the vulnerability is very short, so it cannot be reproduced stably.



<span class="line"><!---->By manual review, it is found that the window time triggered by the vulnerability is very short, so it cannot be reproduced stably.<!----></span>

<b class="line"><!---->Problem Description:<!----></b>



<br>





Type of crash

browser process(Sandbox escape)



<span class="line"><!---->browser process(Sandbox escape)<!----></span>

#Analysis



<span class="line"><!---->#Analysis<!----></span>



<br>





1. IndexedDBContextImpl has quota_client_receiver_, quota_client_receiver_ constructor and executes on idb_task_runner_(ThreadPoolForeg) thread AT[1]



<span class="line"><!---->1. IndexedDBContextImpl has quota_client_receiver_, quota_client_receiver_ constructor and executes on idb_task_runner_(ThreadPoolForeg) thread AT[1]<!----></span>



<br>





2. In the function Bind AT[1], StartReceiving will be called, and the callback function will be set when the connection error occurs AT[2]. Although MultiplexRouter is a thread-safe reference count object, but here use of Unretained to pass this causes the reference count not be incremented correctly.



<span class="line"><!---->2. In the function Bind AT[1], StartReceiving will be called, and the callback function will be set when the connection error occurs AT[2]. Although MultiplexRouter is a thread-safe reference count object, but here use of Unretained to pass this causes the reference count not be incremented correctly.<!----></span>



<br>





3. QuotaContext destructing will cause IndexedDBContextImpl destructing, which will eventually cause quota_client_receiver_ to be freed as well, causing UAF



<span class="line"><!---->3. QuotaContext destructing will cause IndexedDBContextImpl destructing, which will eventually cause quota_client_receiver_ to be freed as well, causing UAF<!----></span>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>

I think the fundamental bug here is that the comment in the IndexedDBContextImpl constructor is incorrect. It says,



<span class="line"><!---->I think the fundamental bug here is that the comment in the IndexedDBContextImpl constructor is incorrect. It says,<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





  // This is safe because the IndexedDBContextImpl must be destructed on the



<span class="line"><!---->  // This is safe because the IndexedDBContextImpl must be destructed on the<!----></span>



<br>





  // IDBTaskRunner, and this task will always happen before that.



<span class="line"><!---->  // IDBTaskRunner, and this task will always happen before that.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





It is not true that this class will always be destroyed on the IDBTaskRunner thread because since it is a reference counted object, whatever thread owns the last reference is the one where it will be destroyed. There is a DCHECK which asserts this assumption but nothing about the architecture which prevents it.



<span class="line"><!---->It is not true that this class will always be destroyed on the IDBTaskRunner thread because since it is a reference counted object, whatever thread owns the last reference is the one where it will be destroyed. There is a DCHECK which asserts this assumption but nothing about the architecture which prevents it.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I think the short-term solution is to modify the callback passed to idb_task_runner_ so it doesn't make assumptions about lifetimes. Longer-term we should migrate away from having objects like IndexedDBContextImpl have ownership passed between threads and instead break it into two objects, each of which are only owned references by a single thread. base::SequenceBound can help with this.



<span class="line"><!---->I think the short-term solution is to modify the callback passed to idb_task_runner_ so it doesn't make assumptions about lifetimes. Longer-term we should migrate away from having objects like IndexedDBContextImpl have ownership passed between threads and instead break it into two objects, each of which are only owned references by a single thread. base::SequenceBound can help with this.<!----></span>

I'm adding Ken here because while the code in IndexedDBContextImpl is a problem I want to make sure that there isn't also an issue in MultiplexRouter. I think the base::Unretained() in StartReceiving() is safe and the problem is that because of the IndexedDBContextImpl bug we're in memory corruption territory that just so happens to make MultiplexRouter do something weird.

The change arichiv@ is working on should fix the potential use-after-free in the lambda from the IndexedDBContextImpl constructor but it doesn't fix the actual bug which triggered this by violating the assumption that IndexedDBContextImpl is always destroyed on the IDB sequence. That issue was introduced by 



<span class="line"><!---->The change arichiv@ is working on should fix the potential use-after-free in the lambda from the IndexedDBContextImpl constructor but it doesn't fix the actual bug which triggered this by violating the assumption that IndexedDBContextImpl is always destroyed on the IDB sequence. That issue was introduced by <!----></span>





https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2594289



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2594289"><!---->https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2594289<!----></a>





 when we stopped having this class be RefCountedDeleteOnSequence.



<span class="line"><!----> when we stopped having this class be RefCountedDeleteOnSequence.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Thinking about that, I think I understand why this crash shows up in MultiplexRouter. By having a mojo::Remote or mojo::Receiver which is bound on the IDB thread (by that lamba) but gets destroyed on the main thread (because of the referencing counting issue) we trigger the intentional thread-unsafety inside these Mojo classes which makes that base::Unretained() a safe assumption.



<span class="line"><!---->Thinking about that, I think I understand why this crash shows up in MultiplexRouter. By having a mojo::Remote or mojo::Receiver which is bound on the IDB thread (by that lamba) but gets destroyed on the main thread (because of the referencing counting issue) we trigger the intentional thread-unsafety inside these Mojo classes which makes that base::Unretained() a safe assumption.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Reporter, does your reproduction case trigger any DCHECKs? We should be catching these broken sequence assumptions in a number of places.



<span class="line"><!---->Reporter, does your reproduction case trigger any DCHECKs? We should be catching these broken sequence assumptions in a number of places.<!----></span>

I don't think the fix actually fixes the use-after-free? It might make it harder to exploit, but if the assumption that IndexedDBContextImpl is always destroyed on the IDB task runner is violated, that also makes any usage of weak_ptr_factory_ no longer valid as the weak pointers will no longer be destroyed on the IDB task runner either, so it is still possible to have a non-null weak ptr while IndexedDBContextImpl has already been destroyed/is in the process of being destroyed.



<span class="line"><!---->I don't think the fix actually fixes the use-after-free? It might make it harder to exploit, but if the assumption that IndexedDBContextImpl is always destroyed on the IDB task runner is violated, that also makes any usage of weak_ptr_factory_ no longer valid as the weak pointers will no longer be destroyed on the IDB task runner either, so it is still possible to have a non-null weak ptr while IndexedDBContextImpl has already been destroyed/is in the process of being destroyed.<!----></span>

While analyzing the stack trace w/ mek, noticed there is something calling a method that ends up calling GetOrCreateBucket with a callback that is bound to the scoped_refptr<IndexedDBContextImpl>. QuotaManager then gets shutdown before the callback is invoked. The suspicion there is that when the callback is not run, the callback is destroyed on the wrong task runner.



<span class="line"><!---->While analyzing the stack trace w/ mek, noticed there is something calling a method that ends up calling GetOrCreateBucket with a callback that is bound to the scoped_refptr&lt;IndexedDBContextImpl&gt;. QuotaManager then gets shutdown before the callback is invoked. The suspicion there is that when the callback is not run, the callback is destroyed on the wrong task runner.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Fixing this here 



<span class="line"><!---->Fixing this here <!----></span>





https://crrev.com/c/3646864



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://crrev.com/c/3646864"><!---->https://crrev.com/c/3646864<!----></a>





 



<span class="line"><!----> <!----></span>

This change updates QuotaManagerProxy to use



<span class="line"><!---->This change updates QuotaManagerProxy to use<!----></span>



<br>





base::BindPostTask to ensure callbacks are run or



<span class="line"><!---->base::BindPostTask to ensure callbacks are run or<!----></span>



<br>





destroyed on the specified task runner. The main difference



<span class="line"><!---->destroyed on the specified task runner. The main difference<!----></span>



<br>





between the existing logic is that if the callback



<span class="line"><!---->between the existing logic is that if the callback<!----></span>



<br>





is never run, it may not be destroyed on the correct task



<span class="line"><!---->is never run, it may not be destroyed on the correct task<!----></span>



<br>





runner. base::BindPostTask makes sure this doesn't happen.



<span class="line"><!---->runner. base::BindPostTask makes sure this doesn't happen.<!----></span>

{M103 PICK} [IndexedDB] Use-After-Free Fix



<span class="line"><!---->{M103 PICK} [IndexedDB] Use-After-Free Fix<!----></span>



<br>

[102] Quota: Use BindPostTask in QuotaManagerProxy



<span class="line"><!---->[102] Quota: Use BindPostTask in QuotaManagerProxy<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This change updates QuotaManagerProxy to use



<span class="line"><!---->This change updates QuotaManagerProxy to use<!----></span>



<br>





base::BindPostTask to ensure callbacks are run or



<span class="line"><!---->base::BindPostTask to ensure callbacks are run or<!----></span>



<br>





destroyed on the specified task runner. The main difference



<span class="line"><!---->destroyed on the specified task runner. The main difference<!----></span>



<br>





between the existing logic is that if the callback



<span class="line"><!---->between the existing logic is that if the callback<!----></span>



<br>





is never run, it may not be destroyed on the correct task



<span class="line"><!---->is never run, it may not be destroyed on the correct task<!----></span>



<br>





runner. base::BindPostTask makes sure this doesn't happen.



<span class="line"><!---->runner. base::BindPostTask makes sure this doesn't happen.<!----></span>



<br>

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.

           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
